<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span></h2>
<div class="was-wotd floatright" style="padding-right: 1em"><span title="This was a Wiktionary Word of the Day"><small><i><a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:Word_of_the_day/Archive/2017/December#12" title="Wiktionary:Word of the day/Archive/2017/December">WOTD – 12 December 2017</a></i></small></span></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#blend" title="Appendix:Glossary">Blend</a> of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/wiki#English" title="wiki">wiki</a></i> +‎ <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dictionary#English" title="dictionary">dictionary</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span></h3>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_English" class="extiw" title="w:British English">UK</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ˈwɪkʃən(ə)ɹi/</span>, <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" class="extiw" title="w:Received Pronunciation">Received Pronunciation</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ˈwɪkʃənɹɪ/</span>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proper_noun">Proper noun</span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">Wiktionary</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/Wiktionaries#English" title="Wiktionaries">Wiktionaries</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A <a href="/wiki/collaborative" title="collaborative">collaborative</a> <a href="/wiki/project#Noun" title="project">project</a> run by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation" class="extiw" title="w:Wikimedia Foundation">Wikimedia Foundation</a> to produce a <a href="/wiki/free#Adjective" title="free">free</a> and <a href="/wiki/complete#Adjective" title="complete">complete</a> <a href="/wiki/dictionary" title="dictionary">dictionary</a> in every <a href="/wiki/language" title="language">language</a>; the dictionaries, collectively, produced by that project.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2003</b> May 1,  Hamish Mackintosh,  “Talk time: William Gibson”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Guardian">The Guardian</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160630144211/https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2003/may/01/interviews.sciencefictionfantasyandhorrorreviews">[1]</a></sup>, London, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2003/may/01/interviews.sciencefictionfantasyandhorrorreviews">the original</a> on <span class="mw-formatted-date" title="2016-06-30">30 June 2016</span>, page 21:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[Hamish Mackintosh:] So is Google officially a verb now? / [<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Gibson" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Gibson">William Gibson</a>:] When I wrote <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_Recognition_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:Pattern Recognition (novel)">Pattern Recognition</a>, it occurred to me that I could use it as a verb and it also occurred to me that someone might already have done so. I thought it didn't matter too much. If I'm first that's great, but if I'm not, then it's just good reportage in a way. Sites like <b>Wiktionary</b> track new usages and neologisms. The page on Google as a verb went back almost two years!</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2008</b>,  Phoebe Ayers; Charles Matthews; Ben Yates,  “Wikimedia Commons and Other Sister Projects”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/How_Wikipedia_Works" class="extiw" title="w:How Wikipedia Works">How Wikipedia Works: And How You Can Be a Part of It</a></cite>, San Francisco, Calif.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_Starch_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:No Starch Press">No Starch Press</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-59327-176-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-59327-176-3">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lHdi1CEPLb4C&amp;pg=PA428">pages 428 and 430</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lHdi1CEPLb4C&amp;pg=PA428">page 428</a>] <b>Wiktionary</b> is a multilingual dictionary (also thesaurus and phrase-book) and has distinctive content policies. Words must be <i>attested</i> and <i>idiomatic</i> (that is, words should be in use, and phrases should be commonly used idioms), and submissions should be neutral and verifiable. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> [<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lHdi1CEPLb4C&amp;pg=PA430">page 430</a>] <b>Wiktionary</b> was proposed on the <i>Wikipedia-L</i> mailing list in April 2001 by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Sanger" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Larry Sanger">Larry Sanger</a>, just three months after Wikipedia was launched. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> An outside project called <i>Omegawiki</i>, started by a handful of Wiktionarians, is working on a grand combination of data from <b>Wiktionary</b> into a single dictionary for all languages.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2008</b>,  John Broughton,  “What Wikipedia is Not”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_%E2%80%93_The_Missing_Manual" class="extiw" title="w:Wikipedia – The Missing Manual">Wikipedia Reader’s Guide</a></cite> (The Missing Manual), Sebastopol, Calif.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O%27Reilly_Media" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:O'Reilly Media">O'Reilly Media</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-596-52174-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-596-52174-5">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Wcob2c_eY48C&amp;pg=PA22">page 22</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Wikipedia has a well-known policy (to experienced editors, at least) stating what kinds of information belong in the encyclopedia. The sister projects that the Wikimedia Foundation supports, such as <b>Wiktionary</b>, fulfill some of the roles that Wikipedia does not. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <b>Wiktionary</b> is a free, multilingual dictionary with definitions, etymologies, pronunciations, sample quotations, synonyms, antonyms and translations. It's the "lexical companion" to Wikipedia.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2010</b>,  Elizabeth Knowles,  “<span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>Appendix:<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span> Where to Look: A Selection of Online Resources”, in  <cite>How to Read a Word</cite>, Oxford: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-957489-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-957489-6">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UYflPqTCIgwC&amp;pg=PA159">page 159</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Collaborative online resources such as <i><b>Wiktionary</b></i> may offer a first view of recent coinages which have not yet been included in traditional dictionaries.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2010</b>,  Christian M. Meyer; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iryna_Gurevych" class="extiw" title="w:Iryna Gurevych">Iryna Gurevych</a>,  “Worth Its Weight in Gold or Yet Another Resource – A Comparative Study of Wiktionary, OpenThesaurus and GermaNet”, in Alexander Gelbukh, editor, <cite>Computational Linguistics and Intelligent Text Processing: 11th International Conference, CICLing 2010, Iasi, Romania, March 21–27, 2010, Proceedings</cite> (Lecture Notes in Computer Science; 6008; LNCS Sublibrary; SL 1 (Theoretical Computer Science and General Issues)), Berlin; Heidelberg; New York, N.Y.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Springer_Science%2BBusiness_Media" class="extiw" title="w:Springer Science+Business Media">Springer</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-642-12115-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-642-12115-9">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lR5rCQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA41">page 41</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The source of a <b>Wiktionary</b> relation is usually associated with a certain word sense. The syntax <i>[2] fish</i> within the article <i>bass</i>, e.g., indicates that the second sense of <i>bass</i> (the fish within the order of Perciformes) is the source of a (hypernymy) relation to the target term <i>fish</i>. Unfortunately, the target of a relation is not sense disambiguated in general, as it is only given by a link to a certain article. For the term <i>fish</i> in the relation above, it is not clear whether the maritime animal, a part of a ship's mast or a card game is meant. Automatic word sense disambiguation is required to determine the correct sense of the target. To our knowledge, this issue has not been addressed in any of the works based on <b>Wiktionary</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  Werner Krauß,  “Heritage and Climate Change: A Fatal Affair”, in David C. Harvey and Jim Perry, editors, <cite>The Future of Heritage as Climates Change: Loss, Adaptation and Creativity</cite> (Key Issues in Cultural Heritage), Abingdon, Oxon.; New York, N.Y.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Routledge" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Routledge">Routledge</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-138-78183-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-138-78183-2">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=zmGhCAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA54">page 54</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">In a letter, Otto Maier called this drawing a "<i>Galimathias</i>"; according to a "<b>wiktionary</b> entry," this is a Greek word that passed from French students to German citizens and signifies something like "nonsense".</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A particular <a href="/wiki/version" title="version">version</a> of this dictionary project, written in a certain language, such as the English-language Wiktionary (often known simply as the English Wiktionary).
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2008</b>,  Phoebe Ayers; Charles Matthews; Ben Yates,  “Wikimedia Commons and Other Sister Projects”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/How_Wikipedia_Works" class="extiw" title="w:How Wikipedia Works">How Wikipedia Works: And How You Can Be a Part of It</a></cite>, San Francisco, Calif.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_Starch_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:No Starch Press">No Starch Press</a>, <small><a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-59327-176-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-59327-176-3">→ISBN</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lHdi1CEPLb4C&amp;pg=PA430">page 430</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The site was brought online in English on December 12, 2002; on March 29, 2004, the first non-English <b>Wiktionaries</b> were initiated in French and Polish. <b>Wiktionaries</b> in over 200 languages now exist, and more than 100 have more than 100 definitions.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
